## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: The target is a population rate equation dP_dt as a function of time t and population size P, which is the standard setup for single-species population dynamics. Common relationships encode density-independent growth, density dependence (carrying capacity), depensation (Allee effects), harvesting, and time-varying/seasonal environments.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Linear-in-population growth/decline with baseline input: dP_dt = c0 + c1 * P (immigration/emigration plus proportional growth/decay)
- Time-varying intrinsic growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (gradual environmental trend affecting per-capita growth)
- Periodic/seasonal forcing of growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (seasonal birth/death rates)
- Verhulst logistic ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (carrying-capacity limited growth with K = 1/c1)
- Theta-logistic (generalized density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P) ** c2) (flexible crowding strength/shape)
- Gompertz-type density dependence (rate form): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (per-capita growth declines ~log(P))
- Richards / generalized logistic (rate form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P) ** c2) ** c3 (additional shape control of approach to capacity)
- Allee effect (strong depensation): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P - 1) (growth negative at low P; threshold at P = 1/c2)
- Allee effect (smooth rational form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (P / (P + c2)) (reduced growth at low P without a hard threshold)
- Harvesting/removal proportional to population: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (constant per-capita removal added to density dependence)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (fixed catch/harvest independent of P)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-independent growth shows dP_dt proportional to P (straight line through origin when plotting dP_dt vs P).
- Carrying capacity implies a factor that changes sign near a particular P (e.g., (1 - c*P)), producing an equilibrium where dP_dt = 0.
- Overcompensation/strong crowding can be captured by higher-order density terms in P (e.g., -c*P^2, or theta-logistic exponents), steepening decline at high P.
- Gompertz-like regulation corresponds to per-capita growth decreasing approximately linearly with log(P), so dP_dt/P ~ a - b*log(P).
- Allee effects require dP_dt negative at low P and positive at intermediate P, often implemented by an additional factor that is negative below a threshold (e.g., (c*P - 1)) or smoothly reduced via P/(P+c).
- Seasonality is indicated when residuals vs t are periodic; multiplicative sin(c*t) on P models seasonal per-capita rate changes.
- Long-term environmental change or management drift is suggested by monotone trends in time; using (c0 + c1*t) as a multiplier shifts growth rates gradually.
- Harvesting/removal is reflected by subtractive terms: -c (constant yield) lowers dP_dt uniformly; -c*P (proportional harvest) tilts the dP_dt vs P relationship downward.

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: c0*P*sin(c1*t) + c2*P*exp(-c3*t)**

The GT has two terms:
1. `P*sin(c1*t)` ŌĆö a sinusoidal term in t, multiplied by P
2. `P*exp(-c3*t)` ŌĆö an exponential decay term in t, multiplied by P

Key observations:
- Everything is proportional to P (linear in P)
- The time dependence involves `sin(c1*t)` and `exp(-c3*t)`
- These are linearly independent basis functions

Now let me analyze each candidate. The critical question is: can the non-sinusoidal parts of each candidate reproduce `P*exp(-c3*t)`?

**General structure of most candidates:** They have `P*c0*sin(c1*t + c2)` (which can match `P*sin(c1*t)` by setting c2=0) plus other terms. The question is whether those other terms can equal `P*exp(-c3*t)`.

Let me categorize the non-sin basis functions appearing in candidates:

- **Power functions like `(c5+t)^(1/5)`, `t^c6`, `(c5+t)^c6`**: These are NOT equivalent to `exp(-c3*t)` for any constant choices. Power functions and exponentials are linearly independent.
- **Rational functions like `1/(c7*t+c8)`**: NOT equivalent to `exp(-c3*t)`.
- **`sqrt(t+c)`, polynomials in t**: NOT equivalent to `exp(-c3*t)`.
- **`log(c*t+1)`**: NOT equivalent to `exp(-c3*t)`.
- **`exp(c*t)`**: This CAN match `exp(-c3*t)` by choosing the constant appropriately.
- **Terms not proportional to P** (like `c7*exp(c8*t)` without P factor): These break the P-linearity of GT.

Let me check candidates with `exp` terms:

**Candidate 31:** `P*c0*sin(c1*t+c2) + P*c3 + P*c4*t + P*c5*t^c6 + P + c7*exp(c8*t)`
The exp term `c7*exp(c8*t)` is NOT multiplied by P. GT requires `P*exp(...)`. Setting c7=0 eliminates it, but then we can't reproduce the exponential. The remaining P-proportional terms are polynomial/power ŌĆö can't match exp. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 32:** Same issue ŌĆö `c7*exp(c8*t)` not multiplied by P. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 33:** Same issue. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 37:** `P*c0*sin(c1*t+c2) + P*c3 + P*c4*t + P*c5*t^c6 + c7*exp(P*c8)` ŌĆö exp depends on P, not t. **NO MATCH**

**Candidates 47-50:** These have `sqrt(P)*c0` terms (not linear in P), `log(P*c8+1)` terms, or `c*exp(c*t)` not multiplied by P. Setting sqrt(P) coefficient to 0 and log coefficient to 0 is possible, but then the exp terms aren't multiplied by P. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 48:** Has `c5*exp(c6*t)` (not ├ŚP) and `c7*log(P*c8+1)` (not linear in P). **NO MATCH**

Going through ALL candidates systematically: None of them contain a term of the form `P*exp(c*t)`. The exponential terms that appear are either not multiplied by P, or depend on P in the exponent. The non-exponential terms (powers, rationals, logs) cannot reproduce `exp(-c3*t)`.

Every candidate fails because none can reproduce the `P*exp(-c3*t)` basis function.

Candidate 1-50 verdict: All **[NO MATCH]**
